<div id="review_163714523" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/163714523" />
    <a title="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship"><img alt="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325201543p2/5229326.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/163714523?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" href="/user/show/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship">Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=wales">wales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=historical-fantasy">historical-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer163714523" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11842230034760541555">This book came highly recommended, so I’m sorry to say that despite its strengths, it has not inspired me to seek out the 15 sequels.<br/><br/>For a fantasy novel first written in the 80s, this has aged reasonably well, though not so well as another recent find of mine, the wonderful <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1022658.The_Ladies_of_Mandrigyn__Sun_Wolf_and_Starhawk___1_' title='The Ladies of Mandrigyn (Sun Wolf and Starhawk, #1) by Barbara Hambly' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Ladies of Mandrigyn</a>. Daggerspell is listed as epic fantasy, though there’s no more than a hint of an Enemy--as opposed to a mere antagonist--in this volume. While Kerr incorporates some old-fashioned elements (I can’t rem</span>
  <span id="freeText11842230034760541555" style="display:none">This book came highly recommended, so I’m sorry to say that despite its strengths, it has not inspired me to seek out the 15 sequels.<br /><br />For a fantasy novel first written in the 80s, this has aged reasonably well, though not so well as another recent find of mine, the wonderful <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1022658.The_Ladies_of_Mandrigyn__Sun_Wolf_and_Starhawk___1_" title="The Ladies of Mandrigyn (Sun Wolf and Starhawk, #1) by Barbara Hambly" rel="nofollow noopener">The Ladies of Mandrigyn</a>. Daggerspell is listed as epic fantasy, though there’s no more than a hint of an Enemy--as opposed to a mere antagonist--in this volume. While Kerr incorporates some old-fashioned elements (I can’t remember when I last read a fantasy book that actually included elves and dwarves), the plot is an unusual one, with the first half following the same group of main characters through multiple incarnations over the span of four hundred years. The second half focuses in on the “modern-day” plotline, involving the rebellion of a minor lord against his prince.<br /><br />But if the plot is innovative, the characters are standard fantasy creations: Jill, the Exceptional Girl; Rhodry, the Noble Prince; Nevyn, the Wise Old Man; Cullyn, the Swordmaster with a Dark Past. They aren't flat, but they never did much to grab my attention, and while seeing the variations in their love rectangle in their several incarnations was a novelty, I didn’t find said love rectangle nearly interesting enough the first time to want to see it repeated twice more. And the “star-crossed lovers” rationale is used to shortcut through actual relationship development, making it hard for me to care about these supposedly life-altering passions. The rebellion in the latter half of the book interested me more: here the story moves at a brisk pace, with enough political complications to please those who prefer intrigue to fighting in their fantasy. It is also nice to see characters who are reasonably quick on the uptake: when there’s a “no man can kill him” prophecy about an opponent, I worried they’d be lost for half the book, but it only takes a few pages for the guys to appeal to Jill.<br /><br />The story takes place in an alternate version of medieval Wales, and Kerr’s worldbuilding deserves the praise it’s been consistently given; much fantasy takes place in “quasi-medieval” worlds, but this one feels like an authentic medieval setting, as well-researched and thought through as historical fiction. The physical and political details of the world ring true: initially I was surprised, for instance, at the small size of the warbands, but for local chieftains with limited resources at their disposal, the numbers make sense. The dialogue is somewhat stylized, but in a consistent way that gives appropriate flavor to the characters’ speech, and the writing style is adequate.<br /><br />In the end, a competent fantasy with textured worldbuilding, but rather staid character roles and personalities that left me uninspired. While this book has an independent plot arc, it’s clearly the first in a series, with many loose ends and a story that, standing alone, has little resonance. I wouldn’t discourage others from picking this up, particularly those who love long fantasy series, but as for me, I’m unlikely to continue.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11842230034760541555" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It follows a set of characters over centuries through their various rebirths and one character who lives through the whole period. <div id="review_2564382538" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2564382538" />
    <a title="Lexie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/712966-lexie"><img alt="Lexie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478802017p2/712966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2564382538?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lexie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lexie" href="/user/show/712966-lexie">Lexie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/712966-lexie?shelf=first-in-series">first-in-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2564382538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7040928829243750902">You ever read an older book, one that's been around for decades (30ish in this case) and say "If only I'd found you sooner".<br/><br/>DAGGERSPELL is that book for me. I vaguely remember always seeing these books on the shelves at the used book stores I frequented, but it never occurred to me to pick it up. Having read this first one I wonder at why that was. This is basically every single trope I thirsted for as a tween/teen desperately seeking fantasy.<br/><br/>Jill, a young girl who's destined for great things an</span>
  <span id="freeText7040928829243750902" style="display:none">You ever read an older book, one that's been around for decades (30ish in this case) and say "If only I'd found you sooner".<br /><br />DAGGERSPELL is that book for me. I vaguely remember always seeing these books on the shelves at the used book stores I frequented, but it never occurred to me to pick it up. Having read this first one I wonder at why that was. This is basically every single trope I thirsted for as a tween/teen desperately seeking fantasy.<br /><br />Jill, a young girl who's destined for great things and caught between two futures.<br /><br />Cullyn, a gruff merc who wants to deny the future as much as possible because the now is fine.<br /><br />Rhodry, a nobleman who feels aimless but largely wants nothing more then to do the right thing.<br /><br />Nevyn, wise weirdo who probably shouldn't keep all those secrets to himself because let's face it they do no one any good unsaid.<br /><br />All stuck in a fate they all couldn't avoid if they tried.<br /><br />This book, maybe because of when it was written (and revised) feels like my childhood reading Mercedes Lackey, Marjorie Kellogg, Tanya Huff, Janny Wurts and Elizabeth Scarborough. The paperback is old - yellowed, stained and with a very creased binding while retaining that old paperback smell of well worn paper and ink. The pages feel roughly textured and the speech is oddly formal even amongst the common folk and their rough slang.<br /><br />I think nostalgia partially had me enjoying this since some of it bored me (I was more interested in Jill than any of her past lives) and I was somewhat nettled by how casually Cullyn's answer to getting Jill to listen was to slap her. 13 year old Alex wouldn't have even given it a second thought, 34 year Lexie is like WHY YOU TAKE THAT JILL.<br /><br />I do have the next two books in the series so I'll be reading them. It's...a good length long so eventually I might get to them all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7040928829243750902" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/189475802?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ruth Macleod" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ruth Macleod" href="/user/show/5878029-ruth-macleod">Ruth Macleod</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5878029-ruth-macleod?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5878029-ruth-macleod?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer189475802" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6750728751409965852">Book 1 of 15 in total, the first in a long series it has a lot to live up to and a lot to accomplish, however it did just that. Daggerspell is probably one of my favourite books in this series as well as a favourite in general. Set in a sort of celtic time the world Katherine Kerr has created is both detailed and thoroughly real, you can immerse yourself in the culture seamlessly and the way she describes things such as the magic and peoples past lives is wonderfully detailed but still understan</span>
  <span id="freeText6750728751409965852" style="display:none">Book 1 of 15 in total, the first in a long series it has a lot to live up to and a lot to accomplish, however it did just that. Daggerspell is probably one of my favourite books in this series as well as a favourite in general. Set in a sort of celtic time the world Katherine Kerr has created is both detailed and thoroughly real, you can immerse yourself in the culture seamlessly and the way she describes things such as the magic and peoples past lives is wonderfully detailed but still understandable. <br /> The plot surrounds the main characters of Nevyn, Jill, Cullyn and Rhodry. The premiss being that the characters fate (wryd) is linked together throughout all their lives, and when they die, they are destined to be reborn in new lives but their souls will still find each other. Its a great concept and one you cant help but get absorbed in as the souls jump from one life to the next, making the same mistakes and improving others.<br /> Jill as the main female character is wonderful and everything a strong lead should be, she's smart and strong and she makes the perfect character for all people who prefer female leads.<br />Nevyn as the main male lead is a wonderful character that you cant help but feel sorry for and hope he achieves his dream.<br />Would recommend to any fantasy lover.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6750728751409965852" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1006613703?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="I&#39;m Booked" class="user" itemprop="url" name="I&#39;m Booked" href="/user/show/22298251-i-m-booked">I&#39;m Booked</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22298251-i-m-booked?shelf=pure-fantasy">pure-fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1006613703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5201336507875686340">I really enjoyed this book! After reading epic fantasy series by Goodkind, Jordan and Martin I was burnt out by the genre; It seemed like every new book that I tried paled in comparison to the GOT series. Luckily, a fellow lover of fantasy recommended that I check out this series and I'm very glad that I did! I enjoyed it so much that I felt that I had to pay it forward, in the hopes that someone else might read these words and decide to pick up one of the best fantasy novels that I've read in Y</span>
  <span id="freeText5201336507875686340" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this book! After reading epic fantasy series by Goodkind, Jordan and Martin I was burnt out by the genre; It seemed like every new book that I tried paled in comparison to the GOT series. Luckily, a fellow lover of fantasy recommended that I check out this series and I'm very glad that I did! I enjoyed it so much that I felt that I had to pay it forward, in the hopes that someone else might read these words and decide to pick up one of the best fantasy novels that I've read in YEARS, (with the exception of The Game of Thrones, of course.)<br /><br />Daggerspell was a well written novel with well developed characters and an interesting plot line. I loved how Kerr utilized the ideas of karma and reincarnation to develop her wonderfully original world. At times it vaguely reminded me of Cloud Atlas and at other times it reminded me of the Wheel of Time but at no time did it ever lose my interest.<br /><br />Daggerspell invited me into the multiple lives of it's main charters and I enjoyed it so much that I practically put my own life on hold until I had finished it. I've already purchased the next three books in the series and I look forward to revisiting Kerr's world soon!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5201336507875686340" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer993331804" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1726504059934358055">Eh. It's alright. The Deverry universe is essentially Celtic reincarnation role-play fantasy, complete with elves & gnomes, though it also borrows heavily from standard Tolkien tropes. Some parts were good, other parts tedious as hell. The magic & the cheesy elvish stuff was fine (& frankly, I'm surprised how many people are put off by the bad-karma incest -- y'all so squeamish, it's more like Shakespeare than George RR Martin >:P). But the MCs were flat, the pacing was awful, & the lack of chap</span>
  <span id="freeText1726504059934358055" style="display:none">Eh. It's alright. The Deverry universe is essentially Celtic reincarnation role-play fantasy, complete with elves &amp; gnomes, though it also borrows heavily from standard Tolkien tropes. Some parts were good, other parts tedious as hell. The magic &amp; the cheesy elvish stuff was fine (&amp; frankly, I'm surprised how many people are put off by the bad-karma incest -- y'all so squeamish, it's more like Shakespeare than George RR Martin &gt;:P). But the MCs were flat, the pacing was awful, &amp; the lack of chapters made boring scenes even more tedious &amp; unending. By the end I just wanted to finish it &amp; have done. <br /><br />2.5 stars, rounded up 3 for the good bits. <br /><br /><br />EDIT, 2/1/18: Opened the second book, read a few pages, cringed, &amp; added both to the donate bag. My time, space, &amp; patience are limited; I'm definitely not bothering with a series that doesn't hook my attention, let alone fills me with ambivalence.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1726504059934358055" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1608350848" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1608350848" />
    <a title="Sotiris Karaiskos" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos"><img alt="Sotiris Karaiskos" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407195235p2/18940246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1608350848?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sotiris Karaiskos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sotiris Karaiskos" href="/user/show/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos">Sotiris Karaiskos</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10307872-daggerspell">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1608350848" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17668472202930503621">As I have said, I always like to go back to the past of fantasy literature that I greatly appreciate to learn about the roots of all these more modern things that I am very much involved with. So I got to the beginning of this very long series and it looks like I'm going to go a long way in it. Following the traditional recipe and adding her own stuff, the author takes us into a fantasy world that has many similarities to Celtic culture, at least as we imagine it. There we come across a story th</span>
  <span id="freeText17668472202930503621" style="display:none">As I have said, I always like to go back to the past of fantasy literature that I greatly appreciate to learn about the roots of all these more modern things that I am very much involved with. So I got to the beginning of this very long series and it looks like I'm going to go a long way in it. Following the traditional recipe and adding her own stuff, the author takes us into a fantasy world that has many similarities to Celtic culture, at least as we imagine it. There we come across a story that seems to move in circles, following the natural cycle of death and reincarnation, and within this, its protagonists move, consciously or unconsciously trying to avoid the same mistakes and correct injustices from their past lives. However, things are always difficult and such a mission is not easy at a time when opposing forces are struggling to dominate and in this first book we learn only a few things about it, leaving more details to follow.<br /><br />What I liked most about this book is that while the author is moving into the familiar fantasy space, with the magical powers, strange creatures and the constant belligerent situation that plagues this land, she is largely avoiding the beaten track to create a more special story. In it, she puts on some very interesting characters, who have their strengths and weaknesses, their needs and demons, and through the narrative the author makes us approach them, understand their struggle and understand the reasons they made these mistakes. This narrative is made with a very beautiful and quite addictive writing, flowing smoothly, with the appropriate pace to be able to enjoy it, passing through quiet moments that thus gain interest to moments of intensity and action that are always meaningful and from there on to. pages that provide emotion in an effortless way. Of course I can't say that the age of this book does not seem as much water flowed under the bridge since, but the work has a maturity that makes it not that far from anything came later from it and this, in combination with all the rest I mentioned, makes this first book of the series particularly appealing to me and gives me a lot of expectations for the sequel.<br /><br />Όπως έχω πει, πάντα μου αρέσει να επιστρέψω στο παρελθόν της φανταστικής λογοτεχνίας που εκτιμώ ιδιαίτερα για να μαθαίνω για τις ρίζες όλων αυτών των πιο σύγχρονων πραγμάτων με τα οποία ασχολούμαι πάρα πολύ. Έτσι έφτασα στην αρχή αυτής της πολύ μακράς σειράς και από ότι φαίνεται θα προχωρήσω αρκετά σε αυτήν. Η συγγραφέας, ακολουθώντας την παραδοσιακή συνταγή και προσθέτοντας δικά της πράγματα μας μεταφέρει σε έναν φανταστικό κόσμο που έχει πολλές ομοιότητες με τον κέλτικο πολιτισμό, τουλάχιστον όπως τον φανταζόμαστε. Εκεί συναντάμε μία ιστορία που φαίνεται να κινείται σε κύκλους, ακολουθώντας τον φυσικό κύκλο του θανάτου και της μετενσάρκωσης, και μέσα σε αυτούς κινούνται οι πρωταγωνιστές της, προσπαθώντας συνειδητά ή ασυνείδητα να αποφύγουν τα ίδια λάθη και να διορθώσουν αδικίες από τις προηγούμενες ζωές τους. Τα πράγματα, όμως, είναι πάντα δύσκολα και μία τέτοια αποστολή δεν είναι καθόλου εύκολη, την ώρα που αντίπαλες δυνάμεις αγωνίζονται να κυριαρχήσουν και σε αυτό το πρώτο βιβλίο μαθαίνουμε μόνο λίγα πράγματα για αυτό, αφήνοντας περισσότερες λεπτομέρειες για τη συνέχεια.<br /><br /> Αυτό που μου άρεσε περισσότερο σε αυτό το βιβλίο είναι ότι πλένω ενώ η συγγραφέας κινείται στον οικείο χώρο της φαντασίας, με τις μαγικές δυνάμεις, τα περίεργα πλάσματα και τη μόνιμη εμπόλεμη κατάσταση που ταλαιπωρεί αυτή τη γη, σε μεγάλο βαθμό αποφεύγει την πεπατημένη για να δημιουργήσει μία περισσότερο ιδιαίτερη ιστορία. Μέσα σε αυτή βάζει μερικούς πολύ ενδιαφέροντες χαρακτήρες, που έχουν τα προτερήματα τους και τις αδυναμίες τους, τις ανάγκες και τους δαίμονες τους, και μέσα από την αφήγηση συγγραφέας μας κάνει να τους προσεγγίσουμε, να αντιληφθούμε τον αγώνα τους και να καταλάβουμε τους λόγους που έκαναν αυτά τα λάθη. Αυτή η αφήγηση γίνεται με μία πολύ όμορφη και αρκετά εθιστική γραφή, που κυλάει ομαλά, με τον κατάλληλο δίσκο για να μπορέσουμε να την απολαύσουμε, περνώντας από στιγμές ήσυχες που έτσι αποκτούν ενδιαφέρον σε στιγμές έντασης και δράσης που όμως έχουν πάντα ουσία και από κει σε σελίδες που προσφέρουν συγκίνηση με έναν αβίαστο τρόπο. Βέβαια δεν μπορώ να πω ότι δεν φαίνεται η ηλικία αυτού του βιβλίου καθώς από τότε έχει κυλήσει πολύ νερό στο αυλάκι, έχει, όμως, το έργο μία ωριμότητα που το κάνει να μην είναι τόσο μακριά από οτιδήποτε μεταγενέστερο και αυτό, σε συνδυασμό με όλα τα υπόλοιπα που προανέφερα, κάνει αυτό το πρώτο βιβλίο της σειράς να μου είναι ιδιαίτερα ελκυστικό και να μου δημιουργεί πολλές προσδοκίες για τη συνέχεια.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17668472202930503621" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('k+aJ7ciyMuOhRudTU75M2XZns8c50uEK69VKtojNPMyJ9L0qf7WXIdJWnuKy+ZHNGRdoXddZE0az8y5wtltq3g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/RgOugxdnd1v6qPC1mFWesNfEI2aQREImZm5y4BY7zbnCjp9u1o4Hxz62nM3JoturC/LF3TK40TBv90Nvs65JA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6002359476553937088">Born in Ohio, 1944. Moved to San Francisco Bay Area in 1962 and has lived there ever since. Katharine Kerr has read extensively in the fields of classical archeology, and medieval and dark ages history and literature, and these influences are clear in her work. Her epic Deverry series has won widespread praise and millions of fans around the world.</span>
